This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\\n226: // stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\\n227: func RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\\n228: \\tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\\n229: \\tif err != nil {\\n230: \\t\\tpanic(err)\\n231: \\t}\\n232: \\tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\\n233: \\t\\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\\n234: \\t}\\n235: \\tle.Run(ctx)\\n236: }\\n237: \\n238: // GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\\n239: // no leader has yet been observed.\\n240: // This function is for informational purposes. (e.g. monitoring, logs, etc.)\\n241: func (le *LeaderElector) GetLeader() string {\\n242: \\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity\\n243: }\\n244: \\n245: // IsLeader returns true if the last /*\\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\\n52: // your own risk.\\n53: package leaderelection\\n54: \\n55: import (\\n56: \\t\\\"bytes\\\"\\n57: \\t\\\"context\\\"\\n58: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n59: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n60: \\n71: const (\\n72: \\tJitterFactor = 1.2\\n73: )\\n74: \\n75: // NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\\n76: func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\\n77: \\tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\\n78: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\\\")\\n79: \\t}\\n80: \\tif \\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\\n113: \\treturn &le, nil\\n114: }\\n115: \\n116: type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\\n117: \\t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\\n118: \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\\n155: \\t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\\n156: \\t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\\n157: \\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\\n158: \\tReleaseOnCancel bool\\n159: \\n160: \\t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\\n161: \\tName string\\n162: \\n163: \\t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\\n164: \\t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\\n165: \\tCoordinated bool\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: // LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\\n169: // lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\\n170: //\\n171: // possible future callbacks:\\n172: //   - OnChallenge()\\n173: type LeaderCallbacks struct {\\n174: \\t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\\n175: \\tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\\n176: \\t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\\n177: \\t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\\n178: \\t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\\n179: \\t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\\n180: \\tOnStoppedLeading func()\\n181: \\t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\\n182: \\t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\\n183: \\t// leader when the client starts.\\n184: \\tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\\n185: }\\n186: \\n187: // LeaderElector is a leader election client.\\n188: type LeaderElector struct {\\n189: \\tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\\n190: \\t// internal bookkeeping\\n191: \\tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\\n192: \\tobservedRawRecord []byte\\n193: \\tobservedTime      time.Time\\n194: \\t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\\n195: \\t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\\n196: \\t// not yet been reported.\\n197: \\treportedLeader string\\n198: \\n199: \\t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\\n200: \\tclock clock.Clock\\n201: \\n202: \\t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\\n203: \\tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\\n204: \\n205: \\tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\\n206: }\\n207: \\n208: // Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\\n209: // before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\\n210: // stopped holding the leader lease\\n211: func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\\n212: \\tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\\n213: \\tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\\n214: \\n215: \\tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\\n216: \\t\\treturn // ctx signalled done\\n217: \\t}\\n218: \\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\\n219: \\tdefer cancel()\\n220: \\tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\\n221: \\tle.renew(ctx)\\n222: }\\n223: \\n224: // RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\\n225: // fails to validate. (e.g. monitoring, logs, etc.)\\n241: func (le *LeaderElector) GetLeader() string {\\n242: \\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity\\n243: }\\n244: \\n245: // IsLeader returns true if the last observed leader was this client else returns false.\\n246: func (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\\n247: \\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\\n248: }\\n249: \\n250: // acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\\n251: // Returns false if ctx signals done.\\n252: func (le *LeaderElector) \\t\\tcancel()\\n274: \\t}, le.config.RetryPeriod, JitterFactor, true)\\n275: \\treturn succeeded\\n276: }\\n277: \\n278: // renew loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew fails or ctx signals done.\\n279: func (le *LeaderElector) renew(ctx context.Context) {\\n280: \\tdefer le.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\\\"stopped leading\\\")\\n281: \\tctx, cancel := wait.PollUntilContextTimeout(ctx, le.config.RetryPeriod, le.config.RenewDeadline, true, func(ctx context.Context) (done bool, err error) {\\n286: \\t\\t\\t// PollUntilContextTimeout invokes condition Returns true\\n431: // on success else returns false.\\n432: func (le *LeaderElector) tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\\n433: \\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n434: \\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\\n435: \\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\\n436: \\t\\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\\n437: \\t\\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\\n438: \\t\\tRenewTime:            now,\\n439: \\t\\tAcquireTime:          now,\\n440: \\t}\\n441: \\n442: \\t// 1. fast path for the leader to update optimistically assuming that the record observed\\n443: \\t// last time is the current version.\\n444: \\tif le.IsLeader() && le.isLeaseValid(now.Time) {\\n445: \\t\\toldObservedRecord := le.getObservedRecord()\\n446: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldObservedRecord.AcquireTime\\n447: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldObservedRecord.LeaderTransitions\\n448: \\n449: \\t\\terr := le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord)\\n450: \\t\\tif err == nil {\\n451: \\t\\t\\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\\n452: \\t\\t\\treturn true\\n453: \\t\\t}\\n454: \\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Failed to update lease optimistically, falling back to slow path\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n455: \\t}\\n456: \\n457: \\t// 2. obtain or create the ElectionRecord\\n458: \\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\\n459: \\tif err != nil {\\n460: \\t\\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\\n461: \\t\\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Error retrieving lease lock\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n462: \\t\\t\\treturn false\\n463: \\t\\t}\\n464: \\t\\tif err = le.config.Lock.Create(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n21: //\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n29: //\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n37: //\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n41: // availability.\n42: //\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n48: // to master availability.\n49: //\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n52: // your own risk.\n53: package leaderelection\n54: \n55: import (\n56: \t\"bytes\"\n57: \t\"context\"\n58: \t\"fmt\"\n59: \t\"sync\"\n60: \t\"time\"\n61: \n62: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n63: \tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n64: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n65: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n66: \trl \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n67: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n68: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n69: )\n70: \n71: const (\n72: \tJitterFactor = 1.2\n73: )\n74: \n75: // NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n76: func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n77: \tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n78: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n79: \t}\n80: \tif lec.RenewDeadline <= time.Duration(JitterFactor*float64(lec.RetryPeriod)) {\n81: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n82: \t}\n83: \tif lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n84: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n85: \t}\n86: \tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n87: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n88: \t}\n89: \tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n90: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"retryPeriod must be greater than zero\")\n91: \t}\n92: \tif lec.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading == nil {\n93: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStartedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n94: \t}\n95: \tif lec.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading == nil {\n96: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStoppedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n97: \t}\n98: \n99: \tif lec.Lock == nil {\n100: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock must not be nil.\")\n101: \t}\n102: \tid := lec.Lock.Identity()\n103: \tif id == \"\" {\n104: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock identity is empty\")\n105: \t}\n106: \n107: \tle := LeaderElector{\n108: \t\tconfig:  lec,\n109: \t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n110: \t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n111: \t}\n112: \tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n113: \treturn &le, nil\n114: }\n115: \n116: type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\n117: \t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\n118: \tLock rl.Interface\n119: \n120: \t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\n121: \t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n122: \t// last observed ack.\n123: \t//\n124: \t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n125: \t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n126: \t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n127: \t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n128: \t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n129: \t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n130: \t// long waits in the scenario.\n131: \t//\n132: \t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n133: \tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n134: \t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n135: \t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n136: \t//\n137: \t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n138: \tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n139: \t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n140: \t// between tries of actions.\n141: \t//\n142: \t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n143: \tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n144: \n145: \t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n146: \t// events of the LeaderElector\n147: \tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n148: \n149: \t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n150: \t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n151: \tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n152: \n153: \t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n154: \t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n155: \t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n156: \t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n157: \t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n158: \tReleaseOnCancel bool\n159: \n160: \t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n161: \tName string\n162: \n163: \t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n164: \t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n165: \tCoordinated bool\n166: }\n167: \n168: // LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n169: // lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n170: //\n171: // possible future callbacks:\n172: //   - OnChallenge()\n173: type LeaderCallbacks struct {\n174: \t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n175: \tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n176: \t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n177: \t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n178: \t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n179: \t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n180: \tOnStoppedLeading func()\n181: \t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n182: \t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\n183: \t// leader when the client starts.\n184: \tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\n185: }\n186: \n187: // LeaderElector is a leader election client.\n188: type LeaderElector struct {\n189: \tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\n190: \t// internal bookkeeping\n191: \tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\n192: \tobservedRawRecord []byte\n193: \tobservedTime      time.Time\n194: \t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\n195: \t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\n196: \t// not yet been reported.\n197: \treportedLeader string\n198: \n199: \t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\n200: \tclock clock.Clock\n201: \n202: \t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\n203: \tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\n204: \n205: \tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\n206: }\n207: \n208: // Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\n209: // before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\n210: // stopped holding the leader lease\n211: func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n212: \tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n213: \tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\n214: \n215: \tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\n216: \t\treturn // ctx signalled done\n217: \t}\n218: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n219: \tdefer cancel()\n220: \tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\n221: \tle.renew(ctx)\n222: }\n223: \n224: // RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\n225: // fails to validate. \n250: // acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\n251: // Returns false if ctx signals done.\n252: func (le *LeaderElector) acquire(ctx \"client/v3/concurrency/election.go\", \"symbol\": \"Campaign\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Leader Election Implementations Across Kubernetes and etcd\\n\\n### Kubernetes Leader Election (Lease-Based)\\n\\n**Architecture Overview:**\\nKubernetes implements leader election using a lease-based mechanism stored in the Kubernetes API. This approach allows multiple components (scheduler, controller-manager, etc.) to coordinate leadership without requiring consensus protocols like Raft.\\n\\n**Core Implementation Files:**\\n\\n1. **staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go** (432 lines) - The main LeaderElector implementation provides the fundamental leader election logic:\\n   - `LeaderElector.Run()` (line 211): Main entry point that calls `acquire()` and then `renew()`\\n   - `acquire()` (line 252): Continuously attempts to acquire leadership using jittered retry periods\\n   - `renew()` (line 279): Periodically renews the lease while holding leadership\\n   - `tryAcquireOrRenew()` (line 432): Core non-coordinated election logic that:\\n     * Uses optimistic fast-path for current leader (line 444)\\n     * Falls back to slow-path on conflict (line 458)\\n     * Checks lease expiration based on LeaseDurationSeconds (line 480)\\n     * Updates LeaderTransitions counter on leader change (line 492)\\n   - Key timing parameters: LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod (lines 120-143)\\n\\n2. **staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leasecandidate.go** (150+ lines) - Coordinated leader election support:\\n   - `LeaseCandidate` struct (line 46): Manages multiple candidates for a single lease\\n   - `NewCandidate()` (line 72): Creates a LeaseCandidate controller with version information (binaryVersion, emulationVersion)\\n   - Watches for PingTime updates from the coordinated election controller to trigger lease renewal\\n   - Supports alpha feature: CoordinatedLeaderElection (line 70)\\n\\n3. **pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/leaderelection_controller.go** (200+ lines) - Coordinated election controller:\\n   - `Controller` struct (line 63): Observes both Lease and LeaseCandidate objects\\n   - `reconcileElectionStep()` (line 168): Orchestrates leader election decisions\\n   - Monitors all candidates for a lease and selects the best one\\n   - Handles lease creation, updates, and coordination with candidate PingTime\\n\\n4. **pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/election.go** (123 lines) - Election logic and strategy:\\n   - `pickBestLeaderOldestEmulationVersion()` (line 29): Implements OldestEmulationVersion strategy\\n   - `compare()` (line 93): Comparison function that prioritizes:\\n     * Lowest emulation version\\n     * Lowest binary version (if emulation versions equal)\\n     * Oldest creation timestamp (if binary versions equal)\\n   - `isLeaseExpired()` (line 111): Checks if lease has expired based on RenewTime and LeaseDurationSeconds\\n\\n5. **staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go** (155 lines) - Lock abstraction:\\n   - `Interface` (line 81): Defines get/create/update operations for leader election records\\n   - `LeaderElectionRecord` (line 46): Stores HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, RenewTime, AcquireTime, LeaderTransitions, Strategy, PreferredHolder\\n   - Only LeasesResourceLock is currently supported (lines 113-126)\\n\\n**Failover and Re-election Mechanism:**\\n- Non-coordinated: When the current leader fails to renew the lease before LeaseDuration expires, any candidate can attempt to acquire it\\n- Coordinated: The dedicated LeaderElectionController continuously monitors candidates and can signal lease holder to step down via PreferredHolder field\\n- Failover happens through time-based expiration rather than consensus, making it simpler but subject to clock skew\\n- OnNewLeader callback notifies interested parties of leadership changes (line 184)\\n\\n---\\n\\n### etcd Leader Election (Raft-Based)\\n\\n**Architecture Overview:**\\netcd implements leader election as a core feature of the Raft consensus algorithm. Every member participates in Raft and automatically elects a leader through distributed voting, ensuring stronger consistency guarantees.\\n\\n**Core Implementation Files:**\\n\\n1. **server/etcdserver/raft.go** (300+ lines) - Raft node integration with leader tracking:\\n   - `raftNode` struct (line 80): Wraps raft.Node and manages message processing\\n   - `start()` (line 173): Main goroutine that processes Raft Ready messages\\n   - Leader detection and transition (lines 185-206):\\n     * Reads `rd.SoftState.Lead` to identify current leader\\n     * Detects leader changes with `newLeader := rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None && rh.getLead() != rd.SoftState.Lead` (line 186)\\n     * Calls `rh.updateLeadership(newLeader)` for transition handling (line 204)\\n   - Updates Raft state metrics: hasLeader, isLeader (lines 200-202)\\n   - Handles heartbeat timeout detection with contention.TimeoutDetector (line 100, 205)\\n   - Different message handling paths for leader vs follower (lines 238-240 vs 295-300)\\n\\n2. **server/etcdserver/server.go** (2000+ lines) - etcd server and Raft integration:\\n   - `EtcdServer.Leader()` method: Returns current Raft leader ID\\n   - `raftReadyHandler` interface (lines 753-756):\\n     * `updateLead(uint64)`: Updates current leader ID (line 753)\\n     * `updateLeadership(bool)`: Handles leadership transition callbacks (line 754)\\n     * `updateCommittedIndex(uint64)`: Updates applied log index (line 755)\\n   - Leadership transition handler (lines 772-775): Manages lessor and other leader-specific operations\\n   - Cluster membership management: Leader handles node additions, removals, and learner promotions\\n\\n3. **server/config/config.go** (325 lines) - Election timing configuration:\\n   - `ElectionTicks` (line 87): Number of ticks for election timeout\\n   - `TickMs` (line 86): Milliseconds per tick\\n   - `InitialElectionTickAdvance` (line 89): Optimization to fast-forward election ticks on startup\\n   - Election timeout formula: `ElectionTicks * TickMs` milliseconds\\n   - Comments explain cross-datacenter deployment considerations (lines 97-108)\\n   - Default fast-forward logic reduces initial election time (lines 90-95)\\n\\n4. **client/v3/concurrency/election.go** (200+ lines) - Client-side election API:\\n   - `Election` struct (line 30): Manages election state and leader information\\n   - `Campaign()` (line 69): Participate in election by creating a lease under the election prefix\\n   - `Leader()` (line 148): Retrieve current leader's information\\n   - `Resign()`: Release leader position\\n   - Uses etcd's built-in consensus (Raft) for election coordination\\n   - Implements higher-level election semantics on top of Raft\\n\\n5. **server/etcdserver/api/v3election/election.go** (150+ lines) - Server-side election service:\\n   - `electionServer.Campaign()` (line 40): Accepts candidate campaigns\\n   - `electionServer.Leader()` (line 98): Returns current election leader\\n   - Implements gRPC Election service (lines 14-49 in proto file)\\n   - Coordinates with Raft for consistency\\n\\n**Failover and Re-election Mechanism:**\\n- Raft-based: Automatic leader election through distributed voting\\n- When leader fails:\\n  * Followers detect leader failure through absence of heartbeats within election timeout\\n  * Followers increment their term and become candidates\\n  * Candidates request votes from other members (PreVote then actual voting)\\n  * First candidate to receive majority of votes becomes new leader\\n- Election timeout = `ElectionTicks * TickMs` (typically 150ms default)\\n- Network partitions: Minority partition cannot elect new leader\\n- Leader sends periodic heartbeats to maintain leadership\\n- Configuration changes (ConfChange) go through Raft log for consistency\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes Lease | etcd Raft |\\n|--------|------------------|----------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Time-based renewal | Consensus-based voting |\\n| **Storage** | Kubernetes API (backed by etcd) | Raft log (distributed) |\\n| **Consistency** | Eventual (clock-skew tolerant) | Strong (Raft guarantees) |\\n| **Failover Time** | LeaseDuration (default 15s) | ElectionTicks*TickMs (default 150ms) |\\n| **Coordination** | Separate controller + candidates | Built-in to core algorithm |\\n| **Network Partition Resilience** | Minority can still lead | Minority cannot lead |\\n| **Use Case** | Multiple independent leaders | Single cluster-wide leader |\\n\\n### Call Chains\\n\\n**Kubernetes Failover Chain:**\\n1. LeaderElector.Run() initiates election loop\\n2. acquire() attempts to get leadership via tryAcquireOrRenew()\\n3. On success, renew() periodically refreshes lease\\n4. If renew fails (leader down), acquireOrRenew falls back to slow-path and another candidate can acquire\\n5. LeaseCandidate watches for PingTime to trigger renewal for coordinated elections\\n6. Controller.reconcileElectionStep() may signal step-down via PreferredHolder\\n7. OnNewLeader callback fires when leadership transitions\\n\\n**etcd Failover Chain:**\\n1. raftNode.start() enters ready loop\\n2. On leader failure, followers detect missing heartbeats\\n3. Key timing parameters: LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod (lines 120-143)\\n\\n2. **staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leasecandidate.go** (150+ lines) - Coordinated leader election support:\\n   - Watches for PingTime updates from the coordinated election controller to trigger lease renewal\\n   - Supports alpha feature: CoordinatedLeaderElection (line 70)\\n\\n3. **pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/leaderelection_controller.go** (200+ lines) - Coordinated election controller:\\n   - `Controller` struct (line 63): Observes both Lease and LeaseCandidate objects\\n   - `reconcileElectionStep()` (line 168): Orchestrates leader election decisions\\n   - LeaderElector.Run() initiates election loop\\n2. acquire() attempts to get leadership via tryAcquireOrRenew()\\n3. On success, renew() periodically refreshes lease\\n4. If renew fails (leader down), acquireOrRenew falls back to slow-path and another candidate can acquire\\n5. LeaseCandidate watches for PingTime to trigger renewal for coordinated elections\\n6. Controller.reconcileElectionStep() may signal step-down via PreferredHolder\\n7. OnNewLeader callback fires when leadership transitions\\n\\n**etcd Failover Chain:**\\n1. raftNode.start() enters ready loop\\n2. On leader failure, followers detect missing heartbeats\\n3. TimeoutDetector signals election timeout\\n4. Follower transitions to candidate state and calls Campaign()\\n5. Sends RequestVote messages to all other members\\n6. First to get majority becomes leader\\n7. raftReadyHandler.updateLeadership() notifies server of transition\\n8. New leader sends AppendEntries heartbeats to establish authority\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
